  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e5b352d4-6d66-4071-8e02-7fccbab13e4f'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer14794327885943481888"><i>I was born for killing – the gods made me to ruin.</i><br/><br/>At the Convent of Sweet Mercy young girls are raised to be killers.   <span id="freeText14794327885943481888" style="display:none"><i>I was born for killing – the gods made me to ruin.</i><br /><br />At the Convent of Sweet Mercy young girls are raised to be killers. In a few the old bloods show, gifting talents rarely seen since the tribes beached their ships on Abeth. Sweet Mercy hones its novices’ skills to deadly effect: it takes ten years to educate a Red Sister in the ways of blade and fist.<br /><br />But even the mistresses of sword and shadow don’t truly understand what they have purchased when Nona Grey is brought to their halls as a bloodstained child of eight, falsely accused of murder: guilty of worse.<br /><br />Stolen from the shadow of the noose, Nona is sought by powerful enemies, and for good reason. Despite the security and isolation of the convent her secret and violent past will find her out. Beneath a dying sun that shines upon a crumbling empire, Nona Grey must come to terms with her demons and learn to become a deadly assassin if she is to survive…</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28863104-chisholm">chisholm</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Really what is this obsession with female leads and the automatic go to for the romance. asspect. Really! these girls are like 9 to 13 years old. Trai<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Really what is this obsession with female leads and the automatic go to for the romance. asspect. Really! these girls are like 9 to 13 years old. Training to be exceptional killer assasins train with the art of warfare hand to hand and weapons you name it. Romance indeed! That's like the last thing the book had in mind. People please pump your brakes and slow your roll and just simply enjoy the story. honestly if you want romance just brake down and get a romance novel. With some age appropriate people is all i'm requesting. this question made me question all females lead rolls in novels do they always have a romantic element? no wonder boys dont read girl leads books. so my question is are all female lead have books with a romantic element?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1770390794" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1770390794" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770390794?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770390794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9361796528550801662">I just reread this book again today in preparation for starting book 2, and it is just as good as the first time :)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of the Sweet Mercy Convent, Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men.</i>
</blockquote>Man, what a hook.<br/><br/>This is classic Mark Lawrence in that it's extremely violent, unflinchingly bloody, and gives no fucks, which may be bad for anyone who isn't really fond of brutality involving children (seriou</span>
  <span id="freeText9361796528550801662" style="display:none">I just reread this book again today in preparation for starting book 2, and it is just as good as the first time :)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of the Sweet Mercy Convent, Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men.</i>
</blockquote>Man, what a hook.<br><br>This is classic Mark Lawrence in that it's extremely violent, unflinchingly bloody, and gives no fucks, which may be bad for anyone who isn't really fond of brutality involving children (seriously, the first chapter starts with <i>No child truly believes they will be hanged</i> Eeee! EEEEEE!!!) and, well, <i>nuns</i>, but you know me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1404424656ra/10236488.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't know why I'm so excited about children dying, but let's leave the psychoanalysis for another time.<br><br>Remember <i>Harry Potter</i>? When little Harry joyfully leaves Privet Drive to enter a school full of magic and hopefully escare his miserably cousins. This book is kind of like that, only little Nona is 8 years old and is entering a very <i>interesting</i> convent to learn to kill, after having already killed someone at her young age. <br><br>They grow up so fast.<br><br>This book isn't one for wimps. The world development is very intricate, and there is a pretty big cast of characters. It helps that there is a guide at the beginning of the book. For example, there are four Tribes in this book, each of which has their own prized characteristics, and all of whom are sought after for their blood and the potency thereof. I can't describe the world building as anything other than <b>freaking brilliant</b>. It is highly complex and remarkably imagined.<br><br><b>Nona</b> is our main character, an orphaned child sold for the potential of power in her blood; through some...complications, she ended up being almost hanged for murder until she is brought to Sweet Mercy's Convent for Young Girls. From then on, we have a school setting, again, like Harry Potter, but not. I love school settings, and this book did not disappoint me. We are immersed into a very, very close setting full of women and girls, and despite the odd setting, the familiar issues of school and of adolescent are still there; there is plenty of backstabbing, competition, friendship, and even romance (!) among the girls, as they train to be one of the four paths: <br><br>- Holy Sister: maintains the faith<br>- Red Sister: skilled in fighting and stuff<br>- Grey Sister: skilled in shadowy arts and sneaking around<br>- Holy Witch: some magical thingamajig<br><br>You'll be glad to know Lawrence is more articulate than me in explaining these.<br><br>The trouble with most bad-ass <b>female</b> assassin books is that they tend to wimp out. The girl will eventually turn out to:<br><br>1. Not really be an assassin at all<br>2. Develop some bullshit view that LOVE IS THE GREATEST GIFT OF ALL<br><br>That's not true in this book, which is a relief, given her age o_ô. <br><br>I enjoyed this book, as I've enjoyed all the other books by Mark Lawrence books I've read. His style remains consistent, and I love the way he writes.<blockquote>
  <i>Thorn stood without motion, for only when you are truly still can you be the centre. She stood without sound, for only silent can you listen. She stood without fear, for only the fearless can understand their peril.<br><br>Thorn waited. Fearless as flowers, bright, fragile, open to the sky. Brave, as only those who’ve already lost can be.</i>
</blockquote>I really can't emphasize how much I love Lawrence's writing. It is intricate, dramatic, intensely lyrical. It makes combat and death seem like art of the highest order. If I haven't made it amply clear yet, I highly recommend this book.<br><br><i>A copy of this book was given to me by the author for review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9361796528550801662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2027370076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027370076" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027370076?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008152291" href="/book/show/31716900-red-sister">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-sff">adult-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-bi">lgbtq-bi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=disability-rep">disability-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-ff-side">lgbtq-ff-side</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027370076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3083384559723396475">The experience of reading <em>Red Sister</em> is akin to getting onto the wrong train—the story draws you relentlessly in and you can’t see the journey ahead, much less guess what it holds. An equally daunting and exciting interruption of the mundane. Depending on the reader, you might decline the adventure and choose to disembark at the next stop. Or you could stay, drifting, allow yourself to be jolted out of your habits and see it through ‘til the end.<br/><br/>I’m glad I chose the latter.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>“It is important, w</em></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3083384559723396475" style="display:none">The experience of reading <em>Red Sister</em> is akin to getting onto the wrong train—the story draws you relentlessly in and you can’t see the journey ahead, much less guess what it holds. An equally daunting and exciting interruption of the mundane. Depending on the reader, you might decline the adventure and choose to disembark at the next stop. Or you could stay, drifting, allow yourself to be jolted out of your habits and see it through ‘til the end.<br /><br />I’m glad I chose the latter.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of the Sweet Mercy convent Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />From those first lines we're hurled unwary into a world where darkness abounds, where powerful children are traded for money, for favors, where priests are drawn to the lure of power, and where nuns schemed and skirmished, made alliances and broke them, called women to battle and sent them home again.<br /><br />The touchstones of Nona Grey’s life had all been thrown into disarray when she was sold to a childtaker. Or perhaps, it was long before that, when she had been all of three or four years and held bloody hands to her mother and said, “<em>this was inside him</em>.” Or maybe that came long after, when Nona brought down near-death and woe upon Raymel Tacsis for hurting her friend and did not count the cost.<br /><br />Perhaps it was the moment when she was yanked back from the brink of a descending death sentence by Abbess Glass who had seen in her a wild streak that could bloom into something magical if it was only allowed to flourish. Chance, fortune, fate—Nona didn’t really know what name to give to it. Her life was crowded with too many ghosts and all the horror of those memories was bound up in another.<br /><br />Nevertheless, in the space where Nona’s story was gleaning words, <em>legend</em> was among them.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>‘I was born for killing –the gods made me to ruin.’</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>Red Sister</em> is the first book in a three-books series, and so, it falls upon it to do a lot of heavy-lifting. And it succeeds in doing so effortlessly. In spare prose of great clarity (the quotability of this book is staggering), Lawrence builds a vivid, densely believable world with an intriguing confluence of history, politics, religion and culture. His world-building is a labyrinthine sprawl of past, present, and future. The layered narrative across the decades is more like bloody footprints steering you wildly into the dark than a walkway threaded with light burning lines through the reader’s mind. But Lawrence makes it work beautifully: we come to learn about Nona’s past along the other characters as memories are returned to her, unsought, from the ether. My mind was awhirl with thoughts, and, at the center of everything: <strong>the mystery of Nona Grey</strong>.<br /><br />The story takes a while to get in gear, though. Red Sister is opaque in plot and glacial in pace. Large portions of the story involve lengthy accounts of Nona’s classes and extended lectures on the Ancestor. A reader who is expecting a more organic experience might struggle with the style and pacing. But here's the thing: don't be fooled by <em>Red Sister</em>’s meandering plot, the way I nearly was. This novel rewards commitment, and by the time the world's magic grows from a whisper to a scream, what was sluggish has become enthralling. Like the way it’s always quiet just before a thunderclap erupts, the descent-into-hell plotline is splashed out in bright, bold strokes. Revelations about the characters struck me like a hammer blow. And by the book’s end, there is a brimming promise of the world widening even more.<br /><br />The sprawling cast of mostly female characters also springs to life. The villains are frighteningly effective, and the development of the plot in tandem to how the main characters get to know each other is well played out. It’s no easy feat to handle the fraught, delicate balances of teenage female friendships as well as the terror and violence of an imminent war, but Lawrence does so masterly. I relished seeing these girls learning to form bonds with their peers, to empathize with them, to draw strength from each other instead of setting out to destroy each other in ways that a sexist system would benefit from. I’m honestly a huge button when it comes to lady friendships in books and this book new just where to push.<br /><br /><em>Red Sister</em> is also a brilliant and triumphant reworking of the “Chosen One” trope, one that doesn't radically deconstruct it so much as examine, test and explore it more extensively and profoundly. With one thought chasing the next in endless circles, I was snatching at hypotheses, turning them over in my head and promptly dismantling them. I’m very much looking forward to the sequel.<br /><br />I absolutely adored Nona’s character. Her character contains multitudes. Nona is many things. A mixture of indomitableness and vulnerability boils behind her eyes, and there’s a roil beneath her ease that I wanted to see revealed. It was also fascinating how involute and multifaceted her character is: she’s the girl who always wears her heart on her sleeve, like a bright banner to attract the world’s snipers, the girl who holds onto her closed ones with a desperate, almost fear-laced quality and to whom friendships are more sacred than any faith. But she’s also the girl who often surrenders to the deeper pull of darkness, her bloodlust unslaked, letting the rage inside her loose in a spasm of violence, the girl who could never tamp down the beehive thrum of hate and rage and despair. This was Nona Grey's gift, grotesque and marvelous, and absolutely riveting to read about.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>‘Those that burn short burn bright. The shortest lives can cast the longest shadows.’</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />In conclusion, I am a <em>heroine</em> addict. I need leading ladies in order to survive. And this book, with an intriguing magic school setting and an all-female cast of deadly nuns, ticked all my boxes! Highly recommended!<br /><br />⚠️
  <strong> SPOILER </strong>
⚠️<br /><br />My one other quibble with this book is how it treats its only disabled character, Hessa, who steps entirely onto the page and plays a major role in the resolution only to be killed off at the end. I was very disappointed when that happened. Disabled representation is already so scarce in Fantasy and I felt robbed out of a character with an incredible arc and so much potential.<br /><br /><a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/runawaywithdreamthieves" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> | <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">TUMBLR</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3083384559723396475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1799930931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799930931" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799930931?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781101988879" href="/book/show/34020941-red-sister">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Coming-of-age fantasy fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59458347-petrik?shelf=arcs-and-review-copies">arcs-and-review-copies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799930931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4331430281036422029"><i>ARC provided by the publisher—Harper Voyager—in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><b>The magic of rereading <i>Red Sister</i> strikes a gold mine.</b><br/><br/>Other than a few changes or grammatical fix, I rarely rewrite my full review. However, <i>Red Sister</i> merits one because I loved it so much more than my first read; the quality jumped from great to amazing in my criteria. I was pleasantly surprised by this. I decided to reread <i>Red Sister</i> in order to refresh my memory before I continue with the series, I didn’t expect to</span>
  <span id="freeText4331430281036422029" style="display:none"><i>ARC provided by the publisher—Harper Voyager—in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><b>The magic of rereading <i>Red Sister</i> strikes a gold mine.</b><br><br>Other than a few changes or grammatical fix, I rarely rewrite my full review. However, <i>Red Sister</i> merits one because I loved it so much more than my first read; the quality jumped from great to amazing in my criteria. I was pleasantly surprised by this. I decided to reread <i>Red Sister</i> in order to refresh my memory before I continue with the series, I didn’t expect to enjoy it this much and I certainly didn’t realize how much I forgot and failed to appreciate in my first read.<br><br><i>Red Sister</i>, the first installment in Mark Lawrence’s <i>Book of the Ancestor</i> trilogy. The story revolves around Nona Grey, a nine-year-old girl brought and raised to become a killer in the Convent of Sweet Mercy. It usually requires ten years in order to become a Red Sister; a class of Sister specialized in armed &amp; unarmed combat. The majority of the story in the book takes place in the Convent and focuses its narrative on Nona’s coming-of-age story. I loved this book. <i>Red Sister</i> is a character-driven coming-of-age fantasy with a battle/magic school setting. If you’ve read and loved <i>Blood Song</i> by Anthony Ryan, I envision you’ll find a lot of things to love in this book. Friendships, faith, sisterhood, money, life, and death were some of the main themes implemented that I immensely enjoyed reading.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Your death has not been waiting for your arrival at the appointed hour: it has, for all the years of your life, been racing towards you with the fierce velocity of time’s arrow. It cannot be evaded, it cannot be bargained with, deflected or placated. All that is given to you is the choice: meet it with open eyes and peace in your heart, go gentle to your reward. Or burn bright, take up arms, and fight the bitch."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The main story and themes were great but it was the characters that shone. Almost all the characters in the book were female; they were splendidly written. Nona as the main character was simply relatable and compelling to read. Although the narrative was told almost in entirety from her perspective, I found every single side character to have their own clear personality. Nona treats friendship preciously; it’s her life, her treasure and she’ll do anything for her friends. Reading about Nona’s new found friendship and family was endearing. Arabella, Abbess Glass, and the badass Sisters interaction with Nona provided a sense of addiction in the narrative. If I weren’t before, now I’m definitely intrigued to find out how the relationships between the characters will develop in the sequels.<br><br><b>Picture: <i>Nona Grey</i> by Francesca Resta</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551012943i/27111285._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Action scenes were also integral in improving the quality of the book. Bloody, vivid, and well-written; the action sequences were placed at the right time after a superbly build pacing. Plus, instead of one, there were two climax sequences that happened in the book; at the end of the first and second half. I’m just going to say that these two climax sequences were incredible. For example, the votive candle and the Shield Test scene—especially on my first read—made me grit my teeth due to how fantastically written it was.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I have been too young to know, and I have been too old to care. It’s in that oh so narrow slice between that memories are made.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>What made this reread experience so much better? I wasn’t able to appreciate Lawrence’s prose and the world-building this book back then. Sometimes when I finished a book, there’s this feeling that I should’ve loved it more; the problems might lie with me and my mindset rather than the book itself not working out for me. That was me with <i>Red Sister</i>. In my first read, I was dumbfounded and confused by the world-building. I also had a difficult time adjusting myself to Lawrence’s prose back then. Now though, on my reread, I came to realize just how much I missed—especially in world-building aspect—on my first read. In my honest opinion, Lawrence’s prose is not too suitable for new entrants to high fantasy, they’re more difficult to appreciate compared to, let’s say, Sanderson’s highly simplistic prose; I feel like I was able to appreciate and understand it so much more now. The world-building was original and interesting. Taking place in a post-apocalyptic world under a dying sun; unique and destructive magic system originated from an old bloodline; I simply can’t wait to learn more about the world that Lawrence has crafted in this trilogy.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“A book is as dangerous as any journey you might take. The person who closes the back cover may not be the same one that opened the front one. Treat them with respect.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I’m really glad I decided to reread <i>Red Sister</i>. Having finished it almost two years ago, sometimes this book appeared in my mind telling me that I should give it another go one day. I'm super pleased that I did because right now, I think of <i>Red Sister</i> as an amazing beginning to a trilogy. This was the first Mark Lawrence’s book that I read and reread. <b>It has also become the first book by Lawrence that entered my 'favorites' shelf.</b> I'm super excited to find out whether <i>Grey Sister</i> or <i>Holy Sister</i> will topple it. If you're a fan of coming-of-age fantasy with battle/magic school premise, accompanied by well-written female characters and a beautiful literary prose, you really can't go wrong with giving <i>Red Sister</i> a read.<br><br><b>Official release date: April 4th, 2017 (US), April 6th, 2017 (UK)</b><br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781101988879/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><i>The quotes in this review were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/02/24/redsister/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4331430281036422029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2503152242" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503152242" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2503152242?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503152242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2471207719671306133">I've been a fan of Mark Lawrence's gritty 'grimdark' fantasy novels for a long while now, but I think Red Sister may be my favorite. (Sorry, Prince of Thorns. I still adore you.) Elevator pitch? Okay, it's reductive, but imagine Hogwarts as a nunnery that trains young girls to be assassins. The world of Abeth orbits a slowly dying sun. As a result, most of the world is encased in ice except for an ever-shrinking corridor along the equator, where humanity is squeezed together, fighting for surviv</span>
  <span id="freeText2471207719671306133" style="display:none">I've been a fan of Mark Lawrence's gritty 'grimdark' fantasy novels for a long while now, but I think Red Sister may be my favorite. (Sorry, Prince of Thorns. I still adore you.) Elevator pitch? Okay, it's reductive, but imagine Hogwarts as a nunnery that trains young girls to be assassins. The world of Abeth orbits a slowly dying sun. As a result, most of the world is encased in ice except for an ever-shrinking corridor along the equator, where humanity is squeezed together, fighting for survival. A satellite mirror, the "Focus Moon," passes over each night, reflecting the dying sun's concentrated light along the corridor in a losing battle to keep the ice at bay. It's a world in which magic and science co-mingle. Four bloodlines, from the original human inhabitants who came ages before, sometimes manifest themselves in present-day children. Gerants are huge and strong. Hunsa are fast and dexterous. Marjal control shadowy and elemental magic. Quantal have the ability to walk the Path -- pulling on the subatomic strands of the universe's fabric to see the future, connect their minds to others', or even manipulate reality. Our hero Nona Gray is a child from the edges of society, sold into slavery by her own mother for reasons not quite clear. She is about to be hanged by a local constable for a heinous crime when she is rescued -- if 'rescued' is the right word -- by the Abbess of the Sweet Mercy Convent. Nona is taken in, and her training begins . . . Fabulous, in-depth world building, great characters, and as always with Lawrence, plotting that is fresh and unpredictable. Upon finishing, I went out immediately and bought the sequel, Gray Sister. If you like fresh, take-no-prisoners fantasy, this is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2471207719671306133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1997564214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1997564214" />
    <a title="Elena May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57120721-elena-may"><img alt="Elena May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581020130p2/57120721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1997564214?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena May" href="/user/show/57120721-elena-may">Elena May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997564214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14750368758160008605"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Are you kidding me with this hook?!?<br/><br/>Is this the best opening sentence in the history of fantasy or what??<br/><br/>Okay, I know. It’s the Prologue. Many books have action-packed prologues that don’t match the rest, so let’s move on to Chapter 1...<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>No child truly believes they will be hanged. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497608985i/23042786.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was my first Mark Lawrence book. I’ve been aware of his works for some time, and he once again got o</span>
  <span id="freeText14750368758160008605" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Are you kidding me with this hook?!?<br><br>Is this the best opening sentence in the history of fantasy or what??<br><br>Okay, I know. It’s the Prologue. Many books have action-packed prologues that don’t match the rest, so let’s move on to Chapter 1...<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>No child truly believes they will be hanged. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497608985i/23042786.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was my first Mark Lawrence book. I’ve been aware of his works for some time, and he once again got on my radar when he became the main A-lister in the <i>Fabulous Fantasy Giveaway</i>. And now I can’t wait to read the rest of his novels!<br><br>I’ve seen many reviewers describe this book as a <b><i>Harry Potter</i> for adults</b>, with lots of blood and gore. On the surface it’s all there – a magic boarding school, wise teachers, four paths the students can take. We even have a poor, orphaned, dark-haired protagonist who is unfamiliar with the magic world, and the rich and blond school nemesis. And the <s>headmaster</s> abbess herself takes a special interest in our protagonist – she brings her to the school under unusual circumstances and supports her with advice and protection. But this is all where the superficial similarities end, and <i>
  <b>nothing about this book feels derivative</b>
</i>. The author never stops playing with the Chosen One trope and takes it to unexpected places!<br><br><b>My favorite thing about this book is the world-building.</b> Abeth is amazing! The focus moon, that allows the Corridor to exist between the blocks of ice! All the different cultures living across the long Corridor! The tribes hunting on the ice, among the ruins left by people who no longer exist! Magic tribes, shiphearts, ships sailing among the stars! I’d love to visit and just travel around though it sounds dangerous and cold. It’s quite intriguing and terrifying how everyone is in a war with everyone, instead of uniting forces to avoid the coming natural disaster, but it’s also very realistic.<br><br>The book has a large cast of characters, and most are well developed, with their own distinguishable personalities. <b>Nona is fascinating</b> – due to her upbringing, she doesn’t understand people, and if you’re her friend, you have to spell it out for her, or else she’ll never know. She’s extremely undiplomatic – she can never pretend to be civil with someone she hates, and is ready to go on a murder spree even if it could lead to an absolute disaster. She’s also strangely devoid of anxiety at some points. If I were her, after arriving at the convent, I’d be driving myself crazy with worry the Tacsis family would be coming, but she doesn’t spare it much thought. I would have liked to see more of her character development happen onscreen. We start with the girl who can’t understand people in Red Class, and move on to someone joking around with the friends in Grey Class, and all of it happens during the gap we never get to see.<br><br>Overall, a solid and enjoyable fantasy novel. Looking forward to the next book in the series!<br><br><b>
  <i>Can you think of a book with a better opening sentence?</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14750368758160008605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2189174665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189174665" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189174665?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189174665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13156266641526797904">Do not mess with these nuns . . . <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513512789ra/24695904.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of Sweet Mercy Convent Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513512789i/24695905._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>No child truly believes they will be hanged. Even on the gallows platform with the rope scratching at their wrists and the shadow of the noose upon their face they know that someone will step forward, a mother, a father returned from some long absence, a king dispensing justice . . . someone. </blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText13156266641526797904" style="display:none">Do not mess with these nuns . . . <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513512789ra/24695904.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of Sweet Mercy Convent Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513512789i/24695905._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>No child truly believes they will be hanged. Even on the gallows platform with the rope scratching at their wrists and the shadow of the noose upon their face they know that someone will step forward, a mother, a father returned from some long absence, a king dispensing justice . . . someone. Few children have lived long enough to understand the world into which they were born. Perhaps a few adults have either, but they at least have learned some bitter lessons.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>First off you must know there are a bunch of jerk holes in this book. Taking children from their homes to sell for different reasons. Mainly to fight for some other jerk in the rings. Children being killed for whatever stupid reason. And there was one part with a horse that pissed me right off and I wanted to kill everyone in the immediate area. But I digress. <br><br>Nona was about to be hanged but she was saved by one of the sisters and carted off to the nun school. Here she will train with the best and become what she is to become. You find out if you have powers and what you will actually be. Killing with poison, a stealer, a flat out killer with blades, your mind, etc and so on. <br><br>Some of the teachers were beyond bad ass. Sister Tallow for one. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"More importantly you will learn about pain, fear, rage, and control. You will learn how to balance the first three to achieve the fourth. and you will carry those lessons into Grey Class where I will put weapons in your hands and teach you what it is to be a Red Sister. In Grey Class I will teach you how to make the fuckers bleed.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Pretty awesome! <br><br>I'm not going to go into all of the classes etc. Why? because I don't feel like it and spoilers and you can read the book. <br><br>There are mixed reviews on the book. Some people think it was too boring and some loved it. I loved it and you need to decide for YOURSELF what you like. I can't wait for the next book out this coming year! Because I have a feeling that it's going to be the one that takes this to whole new level. Now don't get me wrong, there are some bloody killings in this book but we will get to the main stuff in the other books I do believe. <br><br>Happy Reading! <br><br>Mel ♥<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/12/red-sister-by-mark-lawrence.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1868084373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868084373" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868084373?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=freecopy">freecopy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=books-to-review-q1-2017">books-to-review-q1-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868084373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1030665626812639351">I received an advanced copy of Red Sister from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. I would like to announce my gratitude to Mark Lawrence, Ace and Berkley Publishing Group for this opportunity. <br/> <br/>Throughout this narrative, we flaunt within the mind of and follow the actions of Nona. Our protagonist is a young girl who we are introduced to initially whilst she is awaiting execution via the gallows for killing a renowned pit-fighter. Luckily for Nona, it just so happens that Abbess Glass, w</span>
  <span id="freeText1030665626812639351" style="display:none">I received an advanced copy of Red Sister from Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. I would like to announce my gratitude to Mark Lawrence, Ace and Berkley Publishing Group for this opportunity. <br /> <br />Throughout this narrative, we flaunt within the mind of and follow the actions of Nona. Our protagonist is a young girl who we are introduced to initially whilst she is awaiting execution via the gallows for killing a renowned pit-fighter. Luckily for Nona, it just so happens that Abbess Glass, who manages the Sweet Mercy Convent has taken such an interest in her hardships that she offers her the option of joining the nunnery as a Novice, thus escaping the impending death sentence. A large contingent of the interested parties are not particularly happy with this outcome. Perhaps the reason being that Nona did murder the son of one of the wealthiest and proudest men in the world. The repercussions of this singular act ripple throughout the tale. <br /><br />Nona, a fiery but slightly damaged peasant with talents she doesn't truly understand then finds herself in the establishment where the Sisters of Sweet Mercy frequent. It is here where they train future nuns within certain art forms and most importantly, where all revere the Ancestor. Did I mention that these novices are trained to become some of the deadliest killers in the land for their Holy purposes?<br /><br />"It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of the Sweet Mercy Convent Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men"<br /><br />The nunnery is reminiscent of the magic schools such as those created within The Kingkiller Chronicles and A Wizard of Earthsea. Claustrophobic atmospheres, close friendships, harsh teachers, bizarre traditions, bullies and the ultimate shaping of the raw talents shown by Nona, and others; into what their potential will allow. Nona reminded me of Sonea from the Magician's Trilogy. They are similar with their poor upbringing, attending establishments of special education against the wishes of many influential individuals and also, whispers that they are some kind of "chosen one". This is a lot darker than Trudi Canavan's trilogy. The vein here is more sinister, despondent and Nona's past seems extremely more tortuous than Sonea's did.<br /><br />A large percent of Red Sister is set within the convent. The trials and tribulations here, in some aspects, are similar to youth experienced by all young girls such as making friends, dealing with bullies and disliking teachers amongst other dramas. What isn't similar to our world is that the novices become trained in extreme fighting (using fists, knives and throwing stars), taught about poisons and other skills that readers would describe as magical. The convent also has what is known as the Blade Path, which is a timed assault course like activity which would put army endurance tests to shame. In addition to the antics at the convent, the nuns and novices travel elsewhere in this world should their studies find it befitting, such as training with other youths at The Academy. The escapades elsewhere mainly lead them to the capital city of Verity, however; I will not say much about the storyline when the sisters are "unleashed" from their habitual establishment. A highly intriguing aspect of this book was the ingeniously placed flashback sections regarding Nona's youth prior to being found guilty of murder. Examples include juggling lessons and her being abandoned by her family. Each flashback adds an extra layer to Nona's already intricate, complex and perhaps even notorious character. <br /><br />In Lawrence's envisaged world, the moon is falling, there are two miles high fields of ice encompassing the majority of the globe leaving The Corridor where the action takes place and also, one of the finest "magic-systems" I have ever seen depicted in fantasy. <br /><br />The "magic-system" is labyrinthine in its complexity. I used quotation marks with that phrase as to describe it as being as simplistic as that statement is underwhelming for what has been created. For precision, complexity and potential - the magics are potentially on par with the Warrens used in Malazan and Allomancy in Mistborn. At the moment, as stated, I would say they are on par, however; we have no idea of the full possibilities. We were given glimmers throughout of the extra powers certain characters witnessed without understanding and which they could learn when older to manipulate to their will. It is exciting. There is a good mix of John Woo: Stranglehold like slowdown of time, thought control, mind sharing, walking "The Path" to obtain phenomenal destructive power, Witcher-like tracking senses amongst other talents. The skills they have acquired depend on which of the four legendary Abeth tribes these novices descended from. <br /><br />The fabrication of the abnormal powers seems confusing at first but I believe this is intentional. Nona is of course, in an educational environment and as she learns about the magic, possibilities, poisons and histories of the world, then we as readers learn it also. Our gaps in knowledge are filled as the tale progresses, with the necessary information as Nona learns herself; which equals heightened affinity to our protagonist because we are going through the same learning issues and symptoms. <br /><br />This book has scenes of macabre and harrowing happenings but it will then switch back to a pleasant scene in the Convent's dormitory where Nona, as a 9-year-old is gossiping about the happenings in the nunnery and also chatting to her fellow novices about families and friends as young children would. These scenes brought me metaphorically back down to Earth where I had to put the book down for a second and re-analyse that these girls were that young going through what would make many grown men weak at the bladder. It is a great juxtaposition and unifies Nona's relationship with important characters such as Ara, Hessa, Zole and Clera. <br /><br />The finale of this story was utterly breathtaking. Nona is one of my favourite characters in fiction. Lawrence has created one of the most engaging fantasy worlds that my mind has allowed me to visit. At the finale, the second book is set up exceptionally well. It hit me yesterday that because I have an advanced copy of this, that I have to wait even longer for the second book. That is quite upsetting. When it is released officially I will buy this as it deserves a prime of place on my literal favourite bookshelf in my library. This tale was so extraordinary in my mind that I am questioning my previous ratings of other similar stories in this genre. So, note to authors; if I take a star or two off your rating then it is Mark Lawrence's fault, not mine. <br /><br />James Tivendale x</span>
  <a data-text-id="1030665626812639351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1864751282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864751282" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864751282?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864751282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16627212381838278647">Ah, this is going to be a hard book to review. I have a lot of mixed feelings about Lawrence's latest work and I'm going to try and organize my thoughts as best I can.<br/><br/>What I love most about Lawrence's writing is the fact he's - to be frank - <b>dramatic as fuck</b>. He knows how to create a nail-biting, bloody, on-the-edge-of-your-seat kind of scene. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25895524.Red_Sister__Book_of_the_Ancestor___1_' title='Red Sister (Book of the Ancestor, #1) by Mark Lawrence' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Sister</a> opens with an army coming to kill a nun:<br/><blockquote>
  <i>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16627212381838278647" style="display:none">Ah, this is going to be a hard book to review. I have a lot of mixed feelings about Lawrence's latest work and I'm going to try and organize my thoughts as best I can.<br /><br />What I love most about Lawrence's writing is the fact he's - to be frank - <b>dramatic as fuck</b>. He knows how to create a nail-biting, bloody, on-the-edge-of-your-seat kind of scene. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25895524.Red_Sister__Book_of_the_Ancestor___1_" title="Red Sister (Book of the Ancestor, #1) by Mark Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Sister</a> opens with an army coming to kill a nun:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>It is important, when killing a nun, to ensure that you bring an army of sufficient size. For Sister Thorn of the Sweet Mercy Convent, Lano Tacsis brought two hundred men.</i>
</blockquote><br />Then the novel's timeline takes a step back into the past as we join eight-year-old Nona on her journey from almost being hanged to her time training at Sweet Mercy's Convent for Young Girls, spanning several years. <br /><br />Being someone who grew up alongside Harry Potter, magic boarding school books have a special place in my heart. I love the inevitable jealousies, rivalries and friendships that form between the students. And, hey, it's almost like the four Hogwarts houses because here the girls train to become either Red Sisters, Grey Sisters, Holy Sisters or Holy Witches.<br /><br /><b>The beginning and end of the book are awesome</b>. It opens action-packed and dramatic, and ends likewise. The writing is superb. The more I learned about the world and magic system, the more excited I got to explore it further in the next book. <br /><br />Unfortunately, it was the middle chunk of the book where I felt let down. To be honest, <b>it was just quite... boring</b>. It's a fairly medium-length book, and it's on the shorter side for adult fantasy, and yet it felt so very long. While I enjoyed the various character dynamics and the training/learning for a short while, it quickly became repetitive. Nona and the other sisters-in-training go to lessons, train, talk about the Path, train some more, go to more lessons...<br /><br />I feel like the author has a great story to tell here, and the final quarter is where we get some payoff for the long, dragged-out wait, but for me, it wasn't quite enough. I found myself unfavorably comparing this book with other "dark" and/or "adult" magic school books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764861.Skin_Hunger__A_Resurrection_of_Magic___1_" title="Skin Hunger (A Resurrection of Magic, #1) by Kathleen Duey" rel="nofollow noopener">Skin Hunger</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25036395.The_Queen_of_Blood__The_Queens_of_Renthia___1_" title="The Queen of Blood (The Queens of Renthia, #1) by Sarah Beth Durst" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Blood</a>. I enjoyed both of those more.<br /><br />Also, I found Nona - and the characters in general - to be a little stock. She interests me enough to pique my curiosity in the sequel, but she falls into the <b>same old badass female assassin mold</b> that's become the norm in fantasy. I look forward to her character being more developed in the next book.<br /><br />I will definitely be reading the sequel. The ending drops off of a dramatic cliff and seems to promise many exciting things for the future of this story and world. Despite the pacing issues, it's hard not to want to come back for more of this bloody, nasty drama.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16627212381838278647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1896170593" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896170593" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1896170593?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896170593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7541642536190864145"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490648350i/22330860._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Penguin Random House in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A book is as dangerous as any journey you might take. The person who closes the back cover may not be the same one that opened the front one.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This story surrounds a young girl, given away by her mother and village after a frightful night. Yet, even being given away, our young protagonist, Nona, proves that there will always be room in your heart to love. The children that are given away to be sold are worth as muc</span>
  <span id="freeText7541642536190864145" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490648350i/22330860._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Penguin Random House in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A book is as dangerous as any journey you might take. The person who closes the back cover may not be the same one that opened the front one.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story surrounds a young girl, given away by her mother and village after a frightful night. Yet, even being given away, our young protagonist, Nona, proves that there will always be room in your heart to love. The children that are given away to be sold are worth as much as what is in their blood. There are four tribes in this world, and the purer the blood you have, or the more tribes you have in your blood, makes your worth incredibly more valuable. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What good is holy if it watches my friend die –not because she did something wrong but because her blood wasn’t good enough?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><u>
  <b>Four Tribes that the people in this world can descend from:</b>
</u><br>➽ <b>Gerant</b> - Great size and strength.<br>➽ <b>Hunska</b> - Quick speed.<br>➽ <b>Marjal</b> - The ability to tap into lesser magic.<br>➽ <b>Quantal</b> - The ability to walk the Path and work greater magic.<br><br>Nona is sold and has a lot of potential because of her blood, but after Nona is found guilty of a very violent crime, she is sentenced to death. That is, until she is stolen and taken to Sweet Mercy's Convent for young girls, because her blood and potential should not be wasted. Unfortunately, Nona is harboring secrets that are constantly making her question her worth, no matter what's in her blood. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That’s my secret and my shame. I’m Nona Grey, war is in my veins, and the screams of my enemies are music to me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><u>
  <b>Four Classes in the Convent for the novices to learn as a group:</b>
</u><br>➽ <b>Red Class</b> - Ages 9-12 typically. <br>➽ <b>Grey Class</b> - Ages 13-14 typically. <br>➽ <b>Mystic Class</b> - Ages 15-16 typically. <br>➽ <b>Holy Class</b> - Ages 17-19 typically.<br><br>In ten years, Nona will be educated and taught everything she needs to know in the ways of blade and fist while becoming a Red Sister, but there are going to be many hurdles in her way. This book spans only three of those years, but we already get to see the political, power, and religious problems that will not be ignored or easily fought. <br><br><u>
  <b>Four Paths for the novices to take once they become nuns:</b>
</u><br>➽ <b>Bride of the Ancestor</b>, <i>Holy Sister</i> - Honors the Ancestors and keeps the faith. <br>➽ <b>Martial Sister</b>, <i>Red Sister</i> - Warriors skilled in armed and unarmed combat. <br>➽ <b>Sister of Discretion</b>, <i>Grey Sister</i> - Masters of stealth and potions with shadow work.<br>➽ <b>Mystic Sister</b>, <i>Holy Witch</i> - Walks the Path and manipulates threads.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The hardest lesson I ever learned was that every bad thing you see a friend do to someone else they will someday do to you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story puts such a heavy emphasis on friendship and the importance of believing in others even when you've been hurt in the past. Friendship truly is the constant theme of this story, and how beautiful and cruel it can be. Trust is something we should never give willingly, but it can reap so many beautiful things if you choose to put your trust in the right person. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Truth is an ax. Without judgment it’s swung in great circles, wounding everybody”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><u>
  <b>Four girls whose paths cross regardless of what they wanted:</b>
</u><br>➽ <b>Nona</b> - Our sweet cinnamon roll protagonist. <br>➽ <b>Arabella</b> - From royal blood.<br>➽ <b>Clera</b> - Father/family in great financial trouble.<br>➽ <b>Zole</b> - From the Ice Tribes and the ward of a very powerful woman. <br><br>No one is truly all good; everyone comes with failures and faults. Good people can do terrible things just as easily as bad people can perform righteous miracles. Believing in someone else can be a great treasure or a horrible curse, but believing the bad or the good of yourself can be catastrophic. <br><br>And the writing, oh the writing. This writing is slow and meticulous and meaningful. It's different and unique and reflective on things going on in today's world. It's mesmerizing and lyrical and completely unforgettable. I honestly feel like I could have highlighted this whole book! I will definitely be rereading some of these quotes for the rest of my life.<br><br>For me, this story has seeped its way into my body and embedded itself into my heart. I was unable to put it down, and I still am so invested in Nona's character. Nona is the best character I've read about in years. If there was a way for me to put myself into this story, I would and I would fight by her very side because I believe in her that much. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A juggler once came to my village. He was my first friend.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is a story about a chosen one, but it is done in such a perfect way that you are left constantly questioning what is true and what is false. This isn't your typical chosen one cliché in the slightest. The prophecy in this book is unlike any other you've read, and the battle for the truth is such a treat to read about.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It says that the Ark will open when the four tribes demand it with one voice.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And I mean, ultimately this is a story about magical warrior nuns fighting a war from many different sides! How much more do I need to say to sell you? <br><br>Okay, let's talk for a minute about <i>*holds breath and pauses for dramatic effect*</i> SCHOOL SETTINGS! Most people, like me, in their mid to late twenties, grew up with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80584153" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a> which has bewitched all of us to absolutely love and devour books set in boarding school settings. All the different nuns, with all their different specialties, were so reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80584153" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter</a>, too, that I couldn't help but become addicted to reading this. (Side note: Apple/Mistress Shade is everything I wish Snape was in a Potions Master, and she filled my heart with so much happiness.) <br><br>This story also beautifully features lesbians. In fact, I do not believe we even see a hetero relationship in this book. There are two nuns in this book, who are teachers and obviously together, which no one ever shames or questions, but treats the relationship how it should be treated: as normal. There is also a good discussion on being young and having feelings that you aren't sure are "correct" since the feelings are not of the 'norm" of society. One of the other younger girls in the Convent is discovering she is gay, and the transition of her realization is somewhat painful, but so very important. It is never stated that Nona is gay herself, but I truly feel like she is, and I am so excited for that development that could grow, you have no idea. Let the record state that all I want in my life are lesbians in my high fantasy novels and this portion of the story made me completely biased. Also, thank you Mark Lawrence for making a Convent, for only women and girls, have lesbians, because many other authors would have skipped the obvious and made everyone straight. <br><br>My one and only criticism: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I hope Mark Lawrence proves me wrong in the next book, since we know that this world can prevent someone from "dying", but I was really upset that Hessa died. It wasn't because I loved Hessa, even though I did, it was because she was such a good disability representation. It always feels so awful when authors kill the only "different" member of their cast, and that is truly why I was so sad with Hessa's death. Like I said, hopefully I'm wrong, but as of now I'm so sad that this happened. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Your death has not been waiting for your arrival at the appointed hour: it has, for all the years of your life, been racing towards you with the fierce velocity of time’s arrow. It cannot be evaded, it cannot be bargained with, deflected or placated.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall and needless to say, I loved this. It was so immersive and so all-encompassing. I never wanted to put this book down, and all I want now is the second book. The characters are on a whole other level, the writing is nothing short of phenomenal, and the story is so very captivating and addicting. This book will easily make my "top books of 2017" list. Please, do yourself a favor and pick up this amazing book on April 4th, 2017. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There is, in the act of destruction, a beauty which we try to deny, and a joy which we cannot. Children build to knock down, and though we may grow around it, that need runs in us, deeper than our blood.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7541642536190864145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1921420718" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1921420718?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1921420718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5343072669003019878"><b>100% badass from start to finish.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517006262ra/24940982.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When I think of nuns my mind doesn't immediately leap to a group of violent assassins. <br/>Or, at least, it didn't use to.<br/>Now? Well, now perhaps I'll think twice before I try to put the smackdown on a Sister. Who knows what sort of training they've had or weapons they're hiding under those habits?!<br/><i>You can never be too cautious with those religious types...</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517007849ra/24941107.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So, yeah this is basically a story that centers around a little girl with supernatural Wolverine claws who's tryi</span>
  <span id="freeText5343072669003019878" style="display:none"><b>100% badass from start to finish.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517006262ra/24940982.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I think of nuns my mind doesn't immediately leap to a group of violent assassins. <br>Or, at least, it didn't use to.<br>Now? Well, now perhaps I'll think twice before I try to put the smackdown on a Sister. Who knows what sort of training they've had or weapons they're hiding under those habits?!<br><i>You can never be too cautious with those religious types...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517007849ra/24941107.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, yeah this is basically a story that centers around a little girl with supernatural Wolverine claws who's trying to find her place in the world. She gets sold by her village into slavery, convicted of murder and sentenced to hang, and recruited into the Medival Ninja Nun convent - all by the ripe old age of 9. Make no mistake, this kid is a vicious killer.<br><b>And I loved her so much!</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517009027ra/24941179.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, I can see why some people might want to compare the convent to Hogwarts, but...no. I mean, <i>yes</i> there are kids being trained in a 'school setting' to use different forms of magic, there are friendships and rivalries, and there is a prophecy about a Chosen One who will save the day. <br><i>Yadda, yadda, yadda...</i><br>Still. This is not a retelling of Harry Potter and his band of loyal friends.<br><b>This is a story about a very dangerous, very bloodthirsty little girl...<i>with a heart of gold.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517408550ra/24974138.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't hand out 5 stars very often anymore, but this was a phenomenal book. I'm kind of scared of saying anything about the plot because I'm afraid it might ruin someone else's fun, but I have to mention how much I <i>loved</i> the way Lawrence pulled off those flashforward/flashbacks - whatever you want to call them. They were a brilliant touch that took the reading experience to a whole new level for me.<br><b>Highly Recommended!</b></span>
